  • comment on #876 — @chibenwa, 2026-06-29 21:59

    Good catch — confirmed and fixed.

    The bug: the deletion paged the search index with an offset while concurrently deleting the very events it was paging over. Each delete shifts the result set, so offset += pageSize lands past events that moved down, and some are never deleted. So this was an unstable-offset bug, exactly as you suspected.

    The fix: rather than just making the page size tunable, I went for the alternative you preferred and removed paging entirely. The service now lists events straight from CalDAV via a RFC 4791 calendar-query REPORT (CalendarQuery.ofFilters(), same pattern as CalendarEventsReindexService/AlarmScheduleService), takes the multistatus as a single consistent snapshot, and matches the X-OPENPAAS-BOOKING-LINK property on the returned calendar data. The since filter is now read from the real DTSTAMP of the returned ICS. CalDAV is the source of truth and there is no offset to drift, so the bug is structurally gone. This also drops the CalendarSearchService dependency from the service.

    Since there is no longer any page size, I added a test that deletes 10 booking-link events at once (deleteEventsShouldDeleteAllEventsWhenManyEvents) — the scenario that would have exposed the old paging bug — and it now deletes all 10.

    All 7 tests in BookingLinkEventDeletionTest (+ 29 in BookingLinkUserRoutesTest) pass against the real Sabre DAV container.

  • comment on #887 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-01 14:50

    Analysis

    Root cause

    The reindex-calendar-events task iterates users and resources by streaming an open MongoDB cursor while doing very slow per-item work on it, and the cursor is reaped server-side before the next getMore.

    In CalendarEventsReindexService.reindex(...) the source is:

    Flux.concat(
    userDAO.list().concatMap(user -> collectEvents(...)),          // one open cursor
    resourceDAO.findAll().concatMap(resource -> collectEvents(...))) // another open cursor

    Both MongoDBOpenPaaSUserDAO.list() and MongoDBResourceDAO.findAll() are plain streamed cursors with no batching/timeout tuning:

    • MongoDBOpenPaaSUserDAO.java:158-160 -> Flux.from(database.getCollection(COLLECTION).find())
    • MongoDBResourceDAO.java:96-97 -> Flux.from(collection.find()).map(...)

    The reactive driver (com.mongodb.reactivestreams) reads this cursor batch by batch: it fetches one batch, emits it downstream, and only issues the next getMore once that batch is drained. Draining a batch here is extremely expensive and rate-limited:

    • default calendarsConcurrency = 1 (CalendarEventsReindexTask.java:43) -> users and their calendars are processed sequentially via concatMap;
    • for each item we deleteAll from the search index, hit CalDAV (calendarQueryReportXml), parse ICS, and reindex;
    • the whole indexing pipeline is throttled to eventsPerSecond (ReactorUtils.throttle(), lines 142-145).

    With 26540 events and this sequential/throttled processing, the time spent between two consecutive getMore calls on the user cursor easily exceeds MongoDB's default idle-cursor timeout (cursorTimeoutMillis, 10 minutes). The server then reaps the cursor, and the next getMore fails - exactly the stack trace reported:

    MongoCursorNotFoundException: cursor id ... not found (code 43, CursorNotFound)
  at ...AsyncCommandBatchCursor.lambda$getMoreLoop$2

    This propagates up past the per-user/per-resource onErrorResume handlers (those wrap the inner collectEvents monos, not the outer source Flux), reaches the top-level .onErrorResume at lines 155-158, which logs "Task reindex is incomplete" and returns Task.Result.PARTIAL. That is why the task ends failed/partial even though failedEventCount = 0: the failure is the source cursor dying, not any individual event.

    Fix

    Decouple the slow downstream processing from the live driver cursor. The simplest, robust option is to drain the user/resource listing into memory first, closing the cursor quickly, then process:

    userDAO.list()
    .collectList()
    .flatMapMany(Flux::fromIterable)
    .concatMap(user -> collectEvents(context, user, runningOptions.calendarsConcurrency()))

    (and the same for resourceDAO.findAll()). OpenPaaSUser/Resource are lightweight records and their cardinality is bounded (thousands, not the 26k events), so buffering the list is cheap and eliminates the long-lived cursor entirely.

    Alternatives, if streaming must be preserved:

    • Add .noCursorTimeout(true) to the find() used by list()/findAll() so the server never reaps it (the reactive driver closes it on completion/cancel - but a cancelled/aborted stream risks leaking a cursor).
    • Increase batchSize large enough that a single batch covers the whole collection, so no getMore is ever issued - brittle and bounded by the 16MB batch limit.

    Recommendation: go with collectList() materialization for userDAO.list() and resourceDAO.findAll() inside CalendarEventsReindexService.reindex. It is the least surprising and fully removes the timeout window. Worth adding a regression test asserting the source listing is fully consumed before per-item work begins.

    Generated automatically

  • comment on #895 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-02 19:18

    Analysis

    I confirm the race condition is real, and I want to add some precision on why the sequence guard is bypassed, plus flag a second problem that makes the "obvious" fixes insufficient.

    1. Why the delete bypasses the sequence check

    The per-document sequence guard lives in OpensearchCalendarSearchService#indexWithSequence, via the painless script UPSERT_WITH_SEQUENCE_SCRIPT:

    if (ctx._source.sequence == null || params.sequence > ctx._source.sequence) {
    ctx._source.putAll(params.doc);
}

    The request is built with .scriptedUpsert(false) and .upsert(docMap). With scriptedUpsert(false), the script only runs when the document already exists. When the document is missing, OpenSearch inserts the upsert doc verbatim, without running the script.

    So in the recurring path (CalendarEventHandler#indexEvents):

    1. delete(calendarURL, eventUid) removes every occurrence document for the eventUid.
    2. index(calendarEvents) re-indexes each EventFields — but since the documents were just deleted, every upsert takes the insert-verbatim branch and the sequence > ctx._source.sequence check never executes.

    Result: the sequence guard is fully disabled for recurring events with overridden occurrences, exactly as the issue describes. The onErrorResume(isVersionConflict) in indexEvents does not help either — after a delete there is no existing document, so there is no version conflict to catch.

    2. It is not only reordering — it is also non-atomic + concurrent

    Two aggravating factors beyond the A-then-B reorder example:

    • The consumer processes messages with flatMap(..., DEFAULT_CONCURRENCY) (see doConsumeCalendarEventMessages), so messages for the same eventUid run concurrently.
    • delete().then(index()) is not atomic. Even with in-order delivery, an interleaving like A.delete -> B.delete -> B.index(11) -> A.index(10) (or worse, one that drops documents entirely) is possible.

    For the single-event path this is tolerable because the sequence-guarded upsert plus retryOnConflict(3) converges to the newest sequence. The recurring path has neither protection.

    3. The subtle part: naive per-document guards still resurrect deleted occurrences

    It is tempting to "just guard the delete too" (e.g. delete-by-query with sequence < incoming, then sequence-guarded upsert). That fixes the overwrite case but not the removed-occurrence case:

    • Old state (seq 10) has an overridden occurrence X. New state (seq 11) removes that override.
    • B(11) applies: the X document is gone. Good.
    • Stale A(10) arrives later, re-indexes its occurrence set which still contains X. Since the X document no longer exists, the upsert takes the verbatim-insert branch and resurrects the deleted occurrence.

    The root cause is structural: with one OpenSearch document per occurrence, a missing document is indistinguishable between "new" and "deleted by a newer message", so no per-document guard can reject a stale insert.

    Options

    • (A) Single document per recurring event (recommended for correctness). Store the whole CalendarEvents as one document keyed by eventUid+calendarURL, with occurrences as nested fields for search (inner-hits on query). A single atomic sequence-guarded upsert (reusing UPSERT_WITH_SEQUENCE_SCRIPT with the master/max sequence) then makes the whole update all-or-nothing — no delete, no resurrection, no reorder window. This is the design the issue questions, but it is precisely what makes the guard atomic. Cost: mapping change + search() must project inner-hits back to EventFields.

    • (B) Version-guarded delete + guarded upsert. Cheaper, but only a partial fix: it handles the overwrite race (sections 1/2) yet still suffers the resurrection problem (section 3). Being fully correct would need an additional tombstone / event-version record, which starts to approximate (A) anyway.

    • (C) Serialize per eventUid (groupBy(eventUid).concatMap(...)) to remove intra-instance interleaving. Necessary but not sufficient: it does not reorder by sequence and does not cover multi-instance deployments, so it must still be combined with a version guard.

    My recommendation is (A): it is the only option that closes all three problems (overwrite, non-atomicity, resurrection) without bolting on extra tombstone bookkeeping. If the search-side nested-mapping change is too costly short-term, (B)+(C) narrows the window but should be documented as a mitigation rather than a complete fix.

    Generated automatically

  • comment on #896 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-02 19:21

    Analysis

    Root cause: a degenerate (observance-less) VTIMEZONE

    The failing ICS declares a timezone but with an empty VTIMEZONE body — no STANDARD and no DAYLIGHT sub-component:

    BEGIN:VTIMEZONE
TZID:Europe/Paris
END:VTIMEZONE      <-- line 6

    DTSTART/DTEND then reference this timezone via TZID=Europe/Paris. When ical4j finishes the VTIMEZONE component (hence "Error at line 6", which is exactly the END:VTIMEZONE line) it tries to derive the zone's UTC offset by looking up the applicable/latest Observance. With zero observances that lookup returns null, and ical4j then calls Observance.getRequiredProperty(...) on that null → NullPointerException.

    The exception bubbles up through the ical4j CalendarParser as a ParserException, and is finally wrapped by our code in CalendarUtil.parseIcs:

    } catch (ParserException e) {
    throw new RuntimeException("Error while parsing ICal object", e);
}

    which matches the reported Error while parsing ICal object.

    The CompatibilityHints we enable (RELAXED_PARSING, RELAXED_VALIDATION, …) do not help here: this is not a validation/format error the relaxed modes recover from — it's an NPE thrown deep inside ical4j's timezone-offset resolution. Likewise CustomizedTimeZoneRegistry only rescues unknown TZIDs; here the TZID (Europe/Paris) is a perfectly valid IANA id, the problem is purely the empty inline VTIMEZONE shadowing it.

    Why the task ended failed/partial (and not a crash)

    Parsing happens in CalendarEventsReindexService.collectEvents(...) via CalendarUtil.parseIcs. The failure is caught per-ICS-resource:

    .onErrorResume(e -> {
    LOGGER.error("Error ... ics resource name {}", ..., resourceName, e);
    context.incrementFailedEvent();   // -> failedEventCount
    return Mono.empty();
});

    So each of the 4 corrupt resources increments failedEventCount and is skipped; Context.hasFailures() then makes the whole task report PARTIAL (service L106-L162). That is consistent with the observed failedEventCount: 4, all from the same calendar. Good news: the task correctly isolates and continues; it does not abort.

    Impact to flag: reindex first calls calendarSearchService.deleteAll(...) and then re-collects. Because these 4 events fail to re-parse, they are removed from the search index and never re-added → they silently disappear from search results until the data or the parser is fixed.

    Secondary corruption in the same payload

    The ORGANIZER/ATTENDEE values are doubled: mailto:mailto:abc@domain.ltd. This does not cause the NPE (relaxed parsing tolerates it) but confirms the ICS was written malformed by the producer. PRODID:-//Sabre//... + SUMMARY:testFromNewfront strongly suggests the record was created by a client/front-end that emitted a stub VTIMEZONE and the double-mailto: — i.e. the real defect is on the event-creation / ingestion side, and the DAV store now holds corrupt data.

    Recommendations

    1. Make parseIcs resilient (defensive, recommended). Strip VTIMEZONE components that contain no STANDARD/DAYLIGHT observance before building the Calendar. Europe/Paris is a valid IANA zone, so once the empty inline definition is removed, ical4j resolves the offset from its built-in registry (via CustomizedTimeZoneRegistry) and the event parses cleanly. This protects every consumer of parseIcs, not just reindex.
    2. Fix the source data. Repair (or re-import with a corrected timezone) the 4 affected resources in calendar 667037022b752d0026472254/667037022b752d0026472254, otherwise they stay unindexed after the sanitizer ships too (the sanitizer makes them parseable; it doesn't rewrite the DAV store).
    3. Chase the producer bug. Investigate the creation path that emitted the empty VTIMEZONE + doubled mailto: (event 87e925b3-..., "testFromNewfront"). Preventing malformed writes is the durable fix.
    4. Consider an ical4j upgrade — check whether a newer version already tolerates an observance-less VTIMEZONE instead of NPE-ing.

    A good regression test: feed the exact ICS from this issue through CalendarUtil.parseIcs and assert it yields the VEVENT with a resolved Europe/Paris start instead of throwing.

    Generated automatically

    Good catch @vttranlina — you are right that collapsing on the uid only hid duplicates but never deleted an occurrence dropped from a later update, so a removed overridden occurrence lingered in the index and stayed searchable through its own fields. Your test reproduces exactly that.

    I pushed a fix on top of your test:

    • Prune removed occurrences on index.     • Still race-safe (issue #895). The delete is bounded by the message sequence and excludes the freshly written document ids, so a reordered older message can only ever try to delete documents older than itself and cannot resurrect a stale state. The indexingStaleRecurringMasterShouldNotDowngradeNewerOne case still holds.
    • sequence is now indexed (index: true) so the delete-by-query can match on it; upgrade-instructions.md updated (extra mapping step + note that changing index may require a fresh index).

  • comment on #898 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-03 14:12

    Thanks @chibenwa — I looked into the raised concern.

    On max(SEQUENCE): the fix does not gate indexing on a max(SEQUENCE) of the whole recurring event. Each occurrence (master and every overridden instance) is upserted as its own sequence-guarded document, each carrying its own SEQUENCE, so per-instance sequences are respected independently. max(sequence) is used only as a lower bound to prune occurrences that dropped out of a payload, and never deletes a document we just wrote — so it cannot downgrade a newer per-instance state.

    On searching each VEVENT instance (the "Bob" example): this already works. Each occurrence is indexed as a separate document; the collapse on eventUid only groups documents that matched the query. When a keyword matches only an overridden occurrence (e.g. Bob invited on one instance but absent from the master), the master is not a hit, so the collapse group contains only the override and that override VEVENT is returned. keepMaster collapses to the master only when the master itself is also a match.

    This was already exercised indirectly by removedRecurrenceOccurrenceShouldNotRemainSearchableAfterUpdate (searching a keyword unique to an override returns that override). To pin your exact example I added a dedicated contract test, searchShouldReturnOverriddenOccurrenceWhenOnlyItMatches: a recurring master without Bob + one override with Bob as attendee → searching Bob returns the override occurrence. It runs against both the Memory and OpenSearch implementations.

    Pushed as 2cd862bb. Note: the OpenSearch integration test requires Docker and could not run locally; it relies on CI.

  • comment on #898 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-04 04:20

    Fixed the failing searchShouldReturnOverriddenOccurrenceWhenOnlyItMatches test (OpenSearch backend, build #6).

    Root cause: with the collapse-on-uid approach, a keyword that only matches an overridden occurrence (e.g. Bob invited on a single instance) correctly surfaces that occurrence rather than the master. But the OpenSearch CalendarEventsDocument did not store recurrenceId, so the serialize/deserialize round-trip dropped it — the returned occurrence came back with recurrenceId=Optional.empty instead of Optional[2025-01-03T10:00:00Z], which is exactly what the assertion reported. The Memory backend was unaffected because it keeps the EventFields objects as-is.

    Fix (commit f6fa09f3): store recurrenceId as a non-indexed keyword (same treatment as resourceName) in both CalendarEventsDocument and the index mapping, so an overridden occurrence surfaced by search keeps its recurrenceId.

    public abstract class PublicCalendarRoute extends JMAPRoutes {
    // ... 

    @Override
    public Stream<JMAPRoute> routes() {
        return Stream.of(JMAPRoute.builder()
            .endpoint(endpoint())
            .action((req, res) -> Mono.from(metricFactory.decoratePublisherWithTimerMetric(this.getClass().getSimpleName(), handleRequest(req, res))))
            .corsHeaders());
    }

    protected abstract Mono<Void> handleRequest(req, resp);
}

    Similarily we can share error responses as static methods of a more global ErrorResponses class:

    class ErrorResponses {
    public static Mono<Void> doUnauthorizedMissingJWT(HttpServerResponse response) {
        return response.status(HttpResponseStatus.UNAUTHORIZED)
            .headers(JSON_HEADER)
            .sendByteArray(Mono.fromCallable(() -> ErrorResponse.of(401, "Unauthorized", "JWT is missing or invalid").serializeAsBytes()))
            .then();
    }

    public static Mono<Void> doServerError(HttpServerResponse response, Exception exception) {
        return response.status(HttpResponseStatus.INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR)
            .headers(JSON_HEADER)
            .sendByteArray(Mono.fromCallable(() -> ErrorResponse.of(500, "Server Error", exception.getMessage()).serializeAsBytes()))
            .then();
    }

    // Other meaningfull error responses can be shared here
}

New Issue/PR Conversation Comments

  • comment on #272 — @chibenwa, 2026-06-29 02:10

    Analysis — Refine CLASS = PRIVATE / CONFIDENTIAL

    I went through the current implementation to scope the work against @chibenwa proposal matrix.

    Target behaviour (from the proposal)

    viewer / class PUBLIC PRIVATE CONFIDENTIAL
    Owner read+write read+write read+write
    Public / regular read read free/busy (anonymised) nothing (filtered out)
    Public free-busy free/busy free/busy nothing
    Delegate (read) read read (full) free/busy
    Delegate (write) read+write read+write free/busy
    Participant (ATTENDEE) — — read (full)

    Two distinct mechanisms are required, as the ticket notes: PRIVATE/CONFIDENTIAL anonymises (replace details with a Busy placeholder) vs CONFIDENTIAL-to-public filters out (the object must not appear at all).

    Where the logic lives today

    The single decision point is Utils::isHiddenPrivateEvent() (lib/Utils/Utils.php:258), consumed by Utils::hidePrivateEventInfoForUser() (:192), which rewrites a hidden VEVENT down to SUMMARY: Busy + time/recurrence skeleton (:196-255).

    Current rule: if class is neither PRIVATE nor CONFIDENTIAL -> not hidden; otherwise hidden when getOwner() !== userPrincipal (getSourceOwner for subscriptions).

    So PRIVATE and CONFIDENTIAL are identical, and the only distinction is owner vs not-owner — there is no notion of delegate, participant, or filter-out. This matches the ticket two observations.

    Call sites that route through this logic (all need to honour the refined rules):

    • lib/JSON/Plugin.php:103 (iCal GET) and :215 (multiget/REPORT items)
    • lib/JSON/CalDAV/CalendarObjectHandler.php:345, 460, 526
    • lib/CalDAV/PrivateEventPlugin.php:199 — DAV-layer GET/PROPFIND sanitiser (uses an anonymous mock node exposing only getOwner())
    • lib/Publisher/CalDAV/EventRealTimePlugin.php:310 — pub/sub realtime payloads

    Gaps to close

    1. Delegate detection. Today a delegate sees only Busy on a PRIVATE event; the proposal wants delegates to see full details (PRIVATE) or free/busy (CONFIDENTIAL). The viewer relationship must be resolved from SharedCalendar::getInvites() / getShareAccess() -> ACCESS_READ / ACCESS_READWRITE / ACCESS_FREEBUSY (lib/DAV/Sharing/Plugin.php:11, lib/CalDAV/SharedCalendar.php). Note the mock node in PrivateEventPlugin only carries the owner — it would need the invite/share info too.

    2. PRIVATE != CONFIDENTIAL. Split the decision into an enum-like outcome (SHOW / ANONYMISE / FILTER_OUT) computed from (class, relationship): PRIVATE -> owner & delegates SHOW, everyone else ANONYMISE; CONFIDENTIAL -> owner & participants SHOW, delegates ANONYMISE, everyone else FILTER_OUT.

    3. Participant check (CONFIDENTIAL). Resolve whether the current principal is an ATTENDEE/ORGANIZER of the event. Requires principal->email mapping (see lib/Utils/Principal.php, currently minimal) and matching against ATTENDEE/ORGANIZER values.

    4. Filter-out path. hidePrivateEventInfoForUser() only rewrites; it never drops a VEVENT. For CONFIDENTIAL-to-public we need to (a) omit the object from collection/multiget responses and (b) make a direct GET return 404/403 in PrivateEventPlugin.

    5. Free/busy consistency. The matrix says CONFIDENTIAL shows nothing (not even busy) to public free-busy, but busy to delegates. lib/JSON/FreeBusyPlugin.php does not currently filter by CLASS, so it needs the same relationship-aware filtering — otherwise confidential time leaks via free-busy.

    Suggested approach

    1. Introduce a resolver returning the viewer relationship (owner / delegate-read / delegate-write / participant / other) given calendar node + principal, plus a classificationVisibility(class, relationship) returning SHOW/ANONYMISE/FILTER_OUT. Keep it in Utils so all five call sites share it.
    2. Refactor hidePrivateEventInfoForUser() to apply the outcome per-VEVENT (show / anonymise / remove), and have callers drop the whole object when every component filters out.
    3. Extend PrivateEventPlugin (enrich the mock node with invites; add 404/403 on filter-out for direct GET) and FreeBusyPlugin.
    4. Gate behind a flag (mirroring CALDAV_ORGANIZER_VALIDATION) so backend can ship CONFIDENTIAL ahead of the front, which targets public + private only — confidential can land disabled-by-default.

    Open questions

    • Delegation level for confidential: the proposal gives delegates free/busy only. Is there an intended confidential delegation level that grants full access (the wording without specific confidential access hints at one), or is participant-membership the only way to see confidential details?
    • Free-busy leak: confirm CONFIDENTIAL should be invisible (not even busy) to public free-busy — that is stricter than typical calendaring and worth an explicit decision.
    • Scope now: since the front targets public+private, should this PR fully implement confidential (filter-out + participant + free-busy) or only land the PRIVATE delegate behaviour and stub confidential behind the flag?

    Tests Unit: tests/Utils/UtilsTest.php (already covers hidePrivateEventInfoForUser) — add delegate/participant/confidential cases. Plus the DAV-layer PrivateEventPlugin and integration (IT) tests covering GET / multiget / free-busy across the matrix rows.

  • comment on #403 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-01 14:56

    Analysis: why a filter-less calendar-query REPORT times out while export is fine

    Context

    The failing side is the reindex task in twake-calendar-side-service (linagora/twake-calendar-side-service#887). It enumerates every event of a calendar via:

    calDavClient.calendarQueryReportXml(user.username(), calendarURL, CalendarQuery.ofFilters())

    CalendarQuery.ofFilters() is an empty filter — i.e. a CalDAV calendar-query REPORT with no time-range and no prop-filter, asking for all objects + calendar-data. The MongoCursorNotFoundException (error 43) reported on the James side is a downstream symptom: the caller keeps its own Mongo cursor (iterating users/calendars) open while it waits for Sabre to answer; Sabre is so slow on a big calendar that the idle cursor exceeds its server-side timeout and gets reaped. The real problem to fix is here in esn-sabre: the filter-less REPORT is O(N) round-trips.

    Root cause: N+1 in the vendored calendarQueryReport

    The XML REPORT is handled by Sabre\CalDAV\Plugin::calendarQueryReport() (vendor/sabre/dav/lib/CalDAV/Plugin.php:622):

    $nodePaths = $node->calendarQuery($report->filters);   // 1 query -> list of URIs

foreach ($nodePaths as $path) {
    list($properties) =
        $this->server->getPropertiesForPath($requestUri . '/' . $path, $report->properties);  // <-- one PROPFIND *per event*
    ...
}

    calendarQuery() runs a single Mongo query and returns just the URIs, but then the plugin fetches calendar-data one event at a time via getPropertiesForPath(). Each iteration triggers a separate getCalendarObject() → a separate Mongo lookup. For the user in #887 that is ~26 500 individual Mongo round-trips + 26 500 VObject parses in a single request. That is what blows past every reasonable timeout.

    Why export is fast

    The ICS export path (Sabre\CalDAV\ICSExportPlugin::generateResponse, vendor/.../ICSExportPlugin.php:210) has no filter, so it takes the fast branch:

    $nodes = $this->server->getPropertiesForPath($path, [$calDataProp], 1);  // single Depth:1 fetch

    A single Depth-1 propfind resolves to Calendar::getChildren() → Backend\Mongo::getCalendarObjects($calendarId), i.e. one Mongo query that returns every object with its data. No per-event round-trip, no N+1. Same data, one query instead of N.

    Note esn-sabre already learned this lesson for the JSON report: CalendarObjectService::calendarQueryWithAllData() / getMultipleDAVItemsOptimized() fetch URI + calendardata + etag in a single query ({uri: {$in: [...]}}, see CalendarObjectDAO::findByCalendarIdAndUris). The XML calendar-query REPORT never got that treatment and still goes through the stock per-path Sabre loop.

    Proposed fix

    ESN\CalDAV\Plugin already extends Sabre\CalDAV\Plugin (lib/CalDAV/Plugin.php:19), so we can override calendarQueryReport to batch the data retrieval instead of looping one path at a time:

    • Minimal / low-risk: replace the per-path getPropertiesForPath() loop with a single getPropertiesForMultiplePaths($nodePaths, $report->properties) (exactly what ICSExportPlugin does). This turns N getCalendarObject calls into one getMultipleCalendarObjects ($in query). Behaviour, filtering and output are unchanged.
    • Best: for the common empty-filter case (no post-filter needed — see buildQueryFromFilters, requirePostFilter=false), route straight to the existing calendarQueryWithAllData() so URIs + data come back in a single query and each object is parsed at most once. Fall back to the standard path only when a real post-filter is present.

    Either option removes the N+1 and brings the REPORT in line with export's single-query cost, which should make the reindex complete well within the caller's cursor timeout. On the twake side it would also be worth raising/refreshing the enumeration cursor (noCursorTimeout or smaller batches) as defence in depth, but that's secondary once the REPORT itself is fast.

    I can prepare the calendarQueryReport override with tests if you want to proceed.

    Generated automatically

  • comment on #405 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-01 15:17

    Addressed the review: restored add_header 'Allow' ... at the location / level so it is emitted on every request again, as it was before this PR.

    Rationale: the surfaced bug (#404) is specifically about DAV and X-Sabre-Version (and MS-Author-Via) being duplicated because Sabre emits them on every proxied response. Allow, on the other hand, is only emitted by Sabre on OPTIONS requests — which nginx short-circuits and never forwards to PHP — so keeping it at location level does not duplicate anything.

    The copy of Allow inside the if ($request_method = 'OPTIONS') block is kept as well: nginx disables add_header inheritance as soon as any add_header is present in a nested block, so the OPTIONS 200 response needs it re-declared there to still advertise the allowed methods.

    Net diff is now minimal — only the three genuinely duplicated capability headers are moved to the OPTIONS-only short-circuit.

  • comment on #406 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-01 16:15

    Done — moved all the new calendar-query REPORT overrides out of lib/CalDAV/Plugin.php into a dedicated lib/CalDAV/Report.php class (ESN\CalDAV\Report), as suggested.

    Plugin::calendarQueryReport now only keeps the override entrypoint (Sabre dispatches the REPORT to this method) and delegates to Report, passing the stock implementation as a $fallback closure for the shapes we do not handle (direct object, Depth: 0, …). All the batching / single-query logic (buildCalendarQueryReportResult, canReportFromSingleQuery, buildCalendarQueryReportResultFromSingleQuery, renderCalendarData, getCurrentUserPrincipal) moved verbatim into Report, so behaviour is unchanged. Now-unused imports (DateTimeZone, ICalendarObjectContainer, Reader) were dropped from the Plugin.

    Note: I could not run phpunit/phpcs in this environment (PHP execution is blocked here and the report tests need a Mongo backend), but the change is a pure mechanical extraction with no logic modified, and the existing CalendarQueryReportTest still exercises it through Plugin::calendarQueryReport.

  • comment on #406 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-01 16:22

    Addressed the CodeScene delta-analysis findings on lib/CalDAV/Report.php in b9c612f.

    Rather than suppress them, I refactored the code:

    • Extracted the filter-less fast path into a dedicated SingleQueryReport class. Report::buildCalendarQueryReportResult now just tries SingleQueryReport::tryBuild(...) (which returns null when the report cannot be served from a single query) and otherwise falls back to the batched path. This isolates the two concerns and lowers each module's mean cyclomatic complexity.
    • Removed the two 5-argument methods. buildCalendarQueryReportResult no longer takes $needsJson/$calendarTimeZone; the batched path derives them itself. The old renderCalendarData (5 args) now lives in SingleQueryReport and reads its render context (node/currentUser/sanitizeForDelegate/needsJson) from instance state, so it takes a single $object.
    • Removed the complex conditional in the batched loop: the ($needsJson || $report->expand) && isset(...) guard is now two plain early-return guards.
    • Simplified canReportFromSingleQuery by extracting isMongoSharedCalendar, hasFilters and requestsOnlyServableProperties predicates, bringing it well under the complexity threshold.

    Behaviour is unchanged — the single-query and batched paths produce byte-for-byte identical output; only the code structure moved. CI (phpunit/phpcs) will validate.

    Generated automatically

  • comment on #408 — @hungphan227, 2026-07-02 11:48

    The scenario is very simple (nothing is tricky about ics file):

    A create event and invite B B update PARTSTAT (using PUT) Then 403

    As I understand, the issue come from OrganizerValidationPlugin in which it only compare authenticated user with organizer field in ics file. It is true if authenticated user is organizer. In case authenticated user is attendee and he wants to update his PARTSTAT, this plugin returns 403 (it is supposed to be 204).

    Related PR: https://github.com/linagora/esn-sabre/pull/395

  • comment on #408 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-02 11:52

    Ah ah yes indeed but in that case we shall be able to see that it does not change the actual organizer I presure.

  • comment on #408 — @hungphan227, 2026-07-02 12:07

    Possible solution:

    • On modification of an existing object: fetch the stored copy and allow the PUT if the ORGANIZER is unchanged (the attendee isn't introducing a foreign organizer, just editing their delivered copy — scheduling rules elsewhere already constrain what an attendee may change).

  • comment on #1093 — @chibenwa, 2026-06-29 17:08

    Analysis — x-openpaas-videoconference jCal type retro-compat

    Context: linagora/twake-calendar-integration-tests#280 flips the jCal value type of the x-openpaas-videoconference property from unknown to uri (e.g. ["x-openpaas-videoconference",{},"uri",""]). The backend now normalizes stored events to uri (PUT bodies sending unknown still return 201, and the subsequent GET returns uri). So the frontend must keep working whether the property comes back as unknown, uri, or anything else.

    1. Read / parse path — already format-agnostic ✅

    parseEventProperty (common/src/features/Events/utils/parseCalendarEvent.ts:232) destructures the jCal tuple as const [key, params, , value] = prop — the type element (3rd position) is discarded. The x-openpaas-videoconference handler (:170) only reads value. So unknown, uri, text, etc. all parse identically.

    This is already proven by the existing unit test eventUtils.test.ts:38, which feeds type text and passes. No change required to read both formats.

    2. Write path — hardcodes unknown, still functional ⚠️

    makeVevent (common/src/features/Events/utils/makeVevent.ts:29-33) always emits:

    ['x-openpaas-videoconference', {}, 'unknown', event.x_openpass_videoconference ?? null]

    This is the only 'unknown' literal in the events feature. The backend accepts it (integration tests PUT unknown → 201), so nothing breaks. To match the backend's canonical form it would be cleaner to emit 'uri' and an empty string instead of null, but it is not strictly required for correctness.

    3. Real retro-compat risk — series metadata diff in makeSeriesJCal ⚠️

    detectChangedMetadataFields (common/src/features/Events/transformers/makeSeriesJCal.ts:50-66) compares old vs new master properties with a full JSON.stringify of the whole tuple, including the type element. x-openpaas-videoconference is in METADATA_FIELDS (:19).

    After the backend change, the old master loaded from the server serializes as [...,"uri",""], while the new master built by makeVevent serializes as [...,"unknown",null]. The mismatch is twofold (type uri≠unknown, value ""≠null), so the field is flagged as "changed" on every series edit even when the video link was untouched — triggering needless propagation to all override instances and sequence bumps. (The "" vs null value mismatch likely pre-dates this type change; the type flip just widens the gap.) The existing test EventTransformers.test.tsx:357 only exercises the genuine-change case, so it would not catch this false positive.

    Recommendation

    • Read: nothing to do — type is already ignored. Optionally add a regression test parsing the property with type uri to lock the behavior in.
    • Write: align makeVevent to emit uri + empty string for the canonical form.
    • Series: make the metadata-diff in makeSeriesJCal robust to the type/empty-value representation — either compare only name/params/value (dropping the type element) or normalize both sides — so that a no-op video-link field stops being detected as a change. Add/adjust a test covering "master loaded as uri, edited via unknown writer → no spurious override propagation".

    Net: both formats are already supported on the read path; the concrete work is on the write side (canonical uri) and hardening the series metadata comparison.

  • comment on #1096 — @chibenwa, 2026-06-30 14:57

    @chibenwa Done — moved the fix to the source as you suggested. It is possible, and it is indeed cleaner.

    What changed (commit 7630a3f):

    • UserSlice: organiserData now starts as new userOrganiser() and setUserData reassigns a full-fledged new userOrganiser({ cn, cal_address }) instead of mutating fields on a plain object.
    • getOpenPaasUserData: updateOrganizerData likewise rebuilds a userOrganiser instance (preserving any previously set values when the payload doesn't provide them).
    • makeVevent: reverted the boundary re-wrapping — it now calls event.organizer.asJcal() directly again.
    • store.ts: added user.organiserData to serializableCheck.ignoredPaths, consistent with how event class instances are already handled.

    Why this is sufficient: state.user.organiserData was the only organizer source producing a plain object. Every other path already builds a real instance — parseCalendarEvent, the delegated branch of useEventOrganizer, and moveEventBetweenCalendars. The Redux store is already configured to keep class instances (that's exactly why event organizers/attendees survive with their asJcal()), so a userOrganiser instance placed in organiserData keeps its prototype through the store and reaches makeVevent intact.

    Tests: dropped the makeVevent "plain-object organizer" regression test (no longer the design) and added __test__/features/user/UserSlice.test.ts, which asserts the slice always exposes a userOrganiser instance with a working asJcal() — guarding the original #1095 create-event path at its real origin.

    Local run still blocked by the Node-24 toolchain requirement in this environment; CI exercises the Jest suite.

  • comment on #1096 — @chibenwa, 2026-06-30 15:15

    @chibenwa thanks for spotting the failing test. Fixed in 21e4807.

    Cause: UserSlice.test.ts matches **/*.test.ts, so it runs under the jest node project (no DOM). Importing UserSlice transitively pulls in oidcAuth.ts, which evaluates window.SSO_BASE_URL at module load — hence ReferenceError: window is not defined.

    Fix: added a @jest-environment jsdom docblock to the test file (the exact remedy jest suggests in the error), so window is defined during the import. No production code touched.

  • comment on #1099 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-01 17:36

    Thanks @coderabbitai. I looked into the encodeURIComponent suggestion for resolveUriTemplate and decided not to apply it.

    Every documented usage places the substituted values in the host portion of the URL, not in a path or query segment:

    • https://mail-{workplaceFqdn}
    • https://{workplaceFqdn.localpart}-mail.{workplaceFqdn.domain}
    • https://visio-{localpart}.twake.app/#/bridge
    • https://{workplaceFqdn.localpart}-visio.{workplaceFqdn.domain}/#/bridge

    Percent-encoding is not valid inside a hostname (DNS labels cannot contain %xx escapes), so calling encodeURIComponent on localpart / workplaceFqdn.localpart there would corrupt correct hostnames rather than protect them. The correct encoding depends on where in the URL a value lands (host vs. path vs. query), and that is a decision only the template author can make — the generic helper cannot pick one safely for all callers.

    In practice these values are workplace identifiers used as DNS labels/subdomains, so they are already restricted to URL/DNS-safe characters. Encoding them would introduce breakage without fixing a real scenario.

    For those reasons no code change was made.

    Generated automatically

    <!-- walkthrough_start -->

    Walkthrough

    Changes

    This PR adds deep-link support for opening a calendar event via a /events/:uid URL. A new route renders an EventDeepLink component. A new useOpenEventFromUrl hook reads a pending event UID from sessionStorage, dispatches getEventByUid once user and calendar data are available, resolves the matching event and calendar, and triggers the event preview modal through setter callbacks. CalendarController is wired to invoke this hook with userId, calendars, and modal state setters. Corresponding tests cover the fetchEventByUid and calendarIdFromEventHref API functions, along with the getEventByUid.fulfilled reducer behavior for both matched-event and null-payload scenarios.

    Sequence Diagram(s)

    sequenceDiagram
  participant CalendarController
  participant Hook as useOpenEventFromUrl
  participant SessionStorage
  participant Dispatch
  participant Slice as CalendarSlice

  CalendarController->>Hook: useOpenEventFromUrl(userId, calendars, dispatch, setters)
  Hook->>SessionStorage: getItem(PENDING_EVENT_UID_KEY)
  Hook->>SessionStorage: removeItem(PENDING_EVENT_UID_KEY)
  Hook->>Dispatch: dispatch(getEventByUid({userId, uid})).unwrap()
  Dispatch->>Slice: getEventByUid.fulfilled
  Slice-->>Hook: events, calId
  Hook->>Hook: select event by uid, validate calendar exists
  Hook->>CalendarController: setEventDisplayedId/CalId/Temp, setOpenEventDisplay(true)

    Suggested labels: merge_wanted

  • comment on #1102 — @chibenwa, 2026-07-03 04:09

    Thanks for the QA — I found the cause of that missing crucial event param in calendar 5f50a663.../5f50a663... error.

    The Array(1) logged next to it was the tell: it is the property array of a VTIMEZONE component (just its tzid), not a VEVENT. The uid REPORT response bundles a VTIMEZONE alongside the VEVENT inside the calendar object (data[2]), and extractCalendarEvents was parsing every component there as an event. The VTIMEZONE therefore produced an "event" with no uid/start, hence the error (and no event opened).

    Fix: extractCalendarEvents now skips any component whose type is not vevent, so sibling VTIMEZONE (and other) components are ignored. Added a regression test (__test__/features/Calendars/extractCalendarEvents.test.ts) covering both a plain VEVENT and a VEVENT bundled with a VTIMEZONE.

    Note: the change is type-safe by inspection but the Jest suite still cannot run in my sandbox (default Node v12 vs Jest 30), so I could not execute the new test here.

    Pushed as 2de6ad2.

    Generated automatically

Since baseEvent() now forwards the injected RepetitionObject unchanged, the UNTIL tests exercise that fallback instead of the real create-path contract, which populates repetition through RepetitionObject.fromFormValues(...).     <details> <summary>Suggested fix</summary>

     function baseEvent(overrides: Partial<CalendarEvent> = {}): CalendarEvent {
+  const repetition = overrides.repetition
+    ? new RepetitionObject({
+        ...overrides.repetition,
+        allday: overrides.allday ?? false,
+        timezone: overrides.timezone ?? TZID
+      })
+    : undefined
+
   return {
     uid: 'base-uuid-1234',
     title: 'Test Event',
     start: '2024-06-01T10:00:00',
     end: '2024-06-01T11:00:00',
     timezone: TZID,
     allday: false,
     attendee: [],
-    ...overrides
+    ...overrides,
+    repetition
   } as CalendarEvent
 }

    Consider encoding substituted values.

    localpart and workplaceFqdn are interpolated into the template as raw strings without encodeURIComponent.   • inline comment on PR #1094 — @coderabbitai[bot], 2026-06-29 22:01

    🎯 Functional Correctness | 🟠 Major | ⚡ Quick win

    Use a UTC month window with an exclusive upper bound.

    Line 25 currently builds to as midnight at the start of the last local day of the month, so the request drops every slot later that day. Converting local midnights with toISOString() also shifts the range across UTC boundaries for non-UTC users. Query [first day of month, first day of next month) in UTC instead.

    <details> <summary>Suggested fix</summary>

           try {
         const now = new Date()
-        // First day of current month
-        const from = new Date(
-          now.getFullYear(),
-          now.getMonth(),
-          1
-        ).toISOString()
-        // Day 0 of next month = last day of current month
-        const to = new Date(
-          now.getFullYear(),
-          now.getMonth() + 1,
-          0
-        ).toISOString()
+        const from = new Date(
+          Date.UTC(now.getUTCFullYear(), now.getUTCMonth(), 1)
+        ).toISOString()
+        const to = new Date(
+          Date.UTC(now.getUTCFullYear(), now.getUTCMonth() + 1, 1)
+        ).toISOString()

         await fetchBookingSlots(bookingLinkPublicId, from, to)

    </details>

        const now = new Date()

    🎯 Functional Correctness | 🟠 Major | ⚡ Quick win

    Empty-state handling breaks when today's slots are all in the past.

    visibleSlots is always an array (from filter or slots), so !visibleSlots on Line 36 is always false and never triggers the prompt. More importantly, when selectedDay is today and every slot's start is before now, visibleSlots becomes an empty array while slots.length > 0. In that case the render path at Line 105 (slots.length === 0) does not show the booking.noSlots message, leaving the user with an empty slot list and no feedback.

    Use visibleSlots.length for both the early-return/empty checks.
